google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Coldplay';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"coldplay,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Coldplay</b>
are
a
British
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
music">rock</a>
band
formed
in
1996
by
lead
vocalist
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Martin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Martin">Chris
Martin</a>
and
lead
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Jonny_Buckland?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jonny
Buckland">Jonny
Buckland</a>
at
<a
href="/wiki/University_College_London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="University
College
London">University
College
London</a>
(UCL).<sup
id="cite_ref-all_3-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-all-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
they
formed
under
the
name
Pectoralz,
<a
href="/wiki/Guy_Berryman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guy
Berryman">Guy
Berryman</a>
joined
the
group
as
a
bassist
and
they
changed
their
name
to
Starfish.<sup
id="cite_ref-roach_19_4-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-roach_19-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Will_Champion?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Will
Champion">Will
Champion</a>
joined
as
a
drummer,
backing
vocalist,
and
multi-instrumentalist,
completing
the
line-up.
Manager
<a
href="/wiki/Phil_Harvey_(manager)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Phil
Harvey
(manager)">Phil
Harvey</a>
is
often
considered
an
unofficial
fifth
member.<sup
id="cite_ref-roach_22_5-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-roach_22-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
renamed
themselves
&quot;Coldplay&quot;
in
1998,<sup
id="cite_ref-Band_name_6-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Band_name-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
before
recording
and
releasing
three
EPs;
<i><a
href="/wiki/Safety_(EP)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Safety
(EP)">Safety</a></i>
in
1998,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Brothers_%26_Sisters_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brothers
&amp;
Sisters
(song)">Brothers
&amp;
Sisters</a></i>
as
a
single
in
1999
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Blue_Room_(EP)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Blue
Room
(EP)">The
Blue
Room</a></i>
in
the
same
year.
The
latter
was
their
first
release
on
a
major
label,
after
signing
to
<a
href="/wiki/Parlophone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Parlophone">Parlophone</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-ColdplayParlophone_7-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ColdplayParlophone-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>They
achieved
worldwide
fame
with
the
release
of
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Yellow_(Coldplay_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yellow
(Coldplay
song)">Yellow</a>&quot;
in
2000,
followed
by
their
debut
album
released
in
the
same
year,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Parachutes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Parachutes">Parachutes</a></i>,
which
was
nominated
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Mercury_Prize?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mercury
Prize">Mercury
Prize</a>.
The
band's
second
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/A_Rush_of_Blood_to_the_Head?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Rush
of
Blood
to
the
Head">A
Rush
of
Blood
to
the
Head</a></i>
(2002),
was
released
to
critical
acclaim
and
won
multiple
awards,
including
<i><a
href="/wiki/NME?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NME">NME</a></i>'s
Album
of
the
Year.
They
have
also
come
top
of
the
BBC
Radio
2
poll
of
the
favourite
album
of
all
time.
Their
next
release,
<i><a
href="/wiki/X%26Y?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="X&amp;Y">X&amp;Y</a></i>,
the
best-selling
album
worldwide
in
2005,
was
met
with
mostly
positive
reviews
upon
its
release,
though
some
critics
felt
that
it
was
inferior
to
its
predecessor.
The
band's
fourth
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Viva_la_Vida_or_Death_and_All_His_Friends?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Viva
la
Vida
or
Death
and
All
His
Friends">Viva
la
Vida
or
Death
and
All
His
Friends</a></i>
(2008),
was
produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Brian_Eno?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brian
Eno">Brian
Eno</a>
and
released
again
to
largely
positive
reviews,
earning
several
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Award</a>
nominations
and
wins
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/51st_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="51st
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">51st
Grammy
Awards</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-USAgram08_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-USAgram08-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
24
October
2011,
they
released
their
fifth
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mylo_Xyloto?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mylo
Xyloto">Mylo
Xyloto</a></i>,
which
received
mixed
to
positive
reviews,
topped
the
charts
in
over
34
countries,
and
was
the
UK's
best-selling
rock
album
of
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-NME2012_9-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NME2012-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
March
2014,
they
announced
their
new
album,
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Ghost_Stories_(Coldplay_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ghost
Stories
(Coldplay
album)">Ghost
Stories</a></i>,
will
be
released
on
19
May,
the
same
year.</p>








<p>The
band
has
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Coldplay?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
awards
and
nominations
received
by
Coldplay">won
a
number
of
music
awards</a>
throughout
their
career,
including
eight
<a
href="/wiki/Brit_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brit
Awards">Brit
Awards</a>â€”winning
Best
British
Group
three
times,
five
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Award">MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>
and
seven
Grammy
Awards
from
25
nominations.
Coldplay
have
sold
more
than
60
million
records
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-Independent2012_10-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Independent2012-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Bloomberg2012_11-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Bloomberg2012-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
December
2009,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
readers
voted
the
group
the
fourth-best
artist
of
the
2000s.<sup
id="cite_ref-MTV2009_12-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MTV2009-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
Coldplay
have
been
an
active
supporter
of
various
social
and
political
causes,
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Oxfam?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/Make_Trade_Fair?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Make
Trade
Fair">Make
Trade
Fair</a>
campaign
and
<a
href="/wiki/Amnesty_International?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Amnesty
International">Amnesty
International</a>.
The
group
have
also
performed
at
various
charity
projects
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Band_Aid_20?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Band
Aid
20">Band
Aid
20</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Live_8?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
8">Live
8</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Sound_Relief?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sound
Relief">Sound
Relief</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Hope_for_Haiti_Now:_A_Global_Benefit_for_Earthquake_Relief?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hope
for
Haiti
Now:
A
Global
Benefit
for
Earthquake
Relief">Hope
for
Haiti
Now:
A
Global
Benefit
for
Earthquake
Relief</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Secret_Policeman%27s_Balls?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Secret
Policeman's
Balls">The
Secret
Policeman's
Ball</a>,
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Teenage_Cancer_Trust?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Teenage
Cancer
Trust">Teenage
Cancer
Trust</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

style="overflow:hidden;height:;">

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="History">History</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Coldplay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
History">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Formation_and_first_years_.281996.E2.80.9399.29">Formation
and
first
years
(1996â€“99)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Coldplay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Formation
and
first
years
(1996â€“99)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p><a
href="/wiki/Chris_Martin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Martin">Chris
Martin</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Jonny_Buckland?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jonny
Buckland">Jonny
Buckland</a>
first
met
during
their
<a
href="/wiki/Orientation_week?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Orientation
week"
class="mw-redirect">orientation
week</a>
at
<a
href="/wiki/University_College_London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="University
College
London">University
College
London</a>
(UCL)
in
September
1996.
The
pair
spent
the
rest
of
the
university
year
planning
a
band,
ultimately
forming
a
group
called
Pectoralz.<sup
id="cite_ref-all_3-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-all-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Guy_Berryman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guy
Berryman">Guy
Berryman</a>,
a
classmate
of
Martin
and
Buckland,
later
joined
the
group.
By
1997,
the
group,
who
had
renamed
themselves
Starfish,
performed
gigs
for
local
<a
href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Camden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="London
Borough
of
Camden">Camden</a>
promoters
at
small
clubs.<sup
id="cite_ref-roach_19_4-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-roach_19-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
Martin
also
had
recruited
his
longtime
school
friend
<a
href="/wiki/Phil_Harvey_(manager)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Phil
Harvey
(manager)">Phil
Harvey</a>,
who
was
studying
<a
href="/wiki/Classics?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Classics">classics</a>
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="University
of
Oxford">University
of
Oxford</a>,
to
be
the
band's
manager.<sup
id="cite_ref-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
Coldplay
have
since
accepted
Harvey
as
the
fifth
member
of
the
group.<sup
id="cite_ref-Band_name_6-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Band_name-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band's
line-up
was
completed
when
<a
href="/wiki/Will_Champion?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Will
Champion">Will
Champion</a>
joined
to
take
up
percussion
duties.
Champion
had
grown
up
playing
piano,
guitar,
bass,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Tin_whistle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tin
whistle">tin
whistle</a>;
he
quickly
learned
the
drums
(despite
having
no
previous
experience).<sup
id="cite_ref-all_3-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-all-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
finally
settled
on
the
name
&quot;Coldplay&quot;
which
was
suggested
by
Tim
Crompton,
a
local
student
who
had
been
using
the
name
for
his
group.<sup
id="cite_ref-Band_name_6-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Band_name-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
By
1997,
Martin
had
also
met
then
Classics
student
<a
href="/wiki/Tim_Rice-Oxley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tim
Rice-Oxley">Tim
Rice-Oxley</a>.
During
a
weekend
on
<a
href="/wiki/Virginia_Water?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Virginia
Water">Virginia
Water</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Surrey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Surrey">Surrey</a>,
they
asked
each
other
to
play
off
their
own
songs
on
the
piano.
Martin,
finding
Rice-Oxley
to
be
talented,
asked
him
to
be
Coldplay's
keyboard
player
but
Rice-Oxley
refused
as
his
own
band,
<a
href="/wiki/Keane_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Keane
(band)">Keane</a>,
was
already
active.
Days
after,
this
event
would
shape
the
second
line-up
of
Keane
and
keep
Coldplay's
unaltered,
thus
leaving
both
bands
as
quartets.<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1998,
the
band
released
500
copies
of
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Safety_(EP)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Safety
(EP)">Safety
EP</a>.</i><sup
id="cite_ref-balance_16-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-balance-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
Most
of
the
discs
were
given
to
record
companies
and
friends;
only
50
copies
remained
for
sale
to
the
public.
In
December
of
that
year,
Coldplay
signed
to
the
independent
label
<a
href="/wiki/Fierce_Panda_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fierce
Panda
Records">Fierce
Panda</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-balance_16-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-balance-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
first
release
was
the
three-track
<i><a
href="/wiki/Brothers_and_Sisters_EP?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brothers
and
Sisters
EP"
class="mw-redirect">Brothers
and
Sisters
EP</a></i>,
which
they
had
quickly
recorded
over
four
days
in
February
1999.<sup
id="cite_ref-balance_16-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-balance-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
completing
their
final
examinations,
Coldplay
signed
to
<a
href="/wiki/Parlophone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Parlophone">Parlophone</a>
for
a
five-album
contract
in
early
1999.<sup
id="cite_ref-ColdplayParlophone_7-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ColdplayParlophone-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
making
their
first
appearance
at
<a
href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glastonbury
Festival">Glastonbury</a>,
the
band
went
into
studio
to
record
a
third
EP
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Blue_Room_(EP)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Blue
Room
(EP)">The
Blue
Room</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
Five
thousand
copies
were
made
available
to
the
public
in
October
<sup
id="cite_ref-roach_28_18-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-roach_28-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
the
single
&quot;Bigger
Stronger&quot;,
received
<a
href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BBC
Radio
1">BBC
Radio
1</a>
airplay.
The
recording
sessions
for
<i>The
Blue
Room</i>
were
tumultuous.
Champion
was
briefly
fired
from
the
band,
but
Martin
later
pleaded
with
him
to
return
after
kicking
him
out,
and
because
of
his
guilt,
went
on
a
drinking
binge.
Eventually,
the
band
worked
out
their
differences
and
put
in
place
a
new
set
of
rules
to
keep
the
group
intact.
Inspired
by
bands
like
<a
href="/wiki/U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2">U2</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/R.E.M.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="R.E.M.">R.E.M.</a>,
Coldplay
decided
that
they
would
operate
as
a
democracy
(and
that
profits
would
be
shared
equally).
Additionally,
the
band
determined
they
would
fire
anyone
who
used
<a
href="/wiki/Hard_and_soft_drugs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hard
and
soft
drugs"
class="mw-redirect">hard
drugs</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-The_Edge_19-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-The_Edge-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Parachutes_.281999.E2.80.932001.29"><i>Parachutes</i>
(1999â€“2001)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Coldplay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
Parachutes
(1999â€“2001)">edit</a>]</span></h3>

&quot;Yellow&quot;
(Coldplay's
first
top
10
hit
single)
went
to
become
one
of
Coldplay's
most
well-known
songs.
It
was
the
second
single
from














<i><a
href="/wiki/Parachutes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Parachutes">Parachutes</a></i>.

<a

</table>








<p>The
band
initially
planned
to
record
their
debut
album
in
the
space
of
two
weeks.
However,
tours
and
other
live
performances
caused
the
recording
to
spread
out
between
September
1999
and
Aprilâ€“May
2000.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
recorded
at
<a
href="/wiki/Rockfield_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rockfield
Studios">Rockfield
Studios</a>,
Matrix
Studios,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Wessex_Sound_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wessex
Sound
Studios">Wessex
Sound
Studios</a>
with
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Ken_Nelson_(British_record_producer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ken
Nelson
(British
record
producer)">Ken
Nelson</a>,
although
the
majority
of
Parachutes'
tracks
were
recorded
at
<a
href="/wiki/Liverpool?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>'s
Parr
Street
Studios
(where
they
accessed
three
studio
rooms).
The
mixing
process
on
all
songs
for
the
album
was
done
by
American
engineer
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Brauer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michael
Brauer">Michael
Brauer</a>
in
New
York.<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
that
period,
they
played
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/NME_Tours?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NME
Tours">Carling
Tour</a>,
which
showcased
up-and-coming
acts.<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
releasing
three
EPs
without
a
hit
song,
Coldplay
sparked
their
first
<a
href="/wiki/Top_40?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Top
40">Top
40</a>
hit
with
the
lead
single
from
<i><a
href="/wiki/Parachutes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Parachutes">Parachutes</a></i>,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Shiver_(Coldplay_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shiver
(Coldplay
song)">Shiver</a>&quot;,
released
in
March
2000
to
a
number
35
peak
position
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Singles
Chart">UK
Singles
Chart</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
June
2000
was
a
pivotal
moment
in
Coldplay's
history:
the
band
embarked
on
their
first
headlining
tour,
including
a
showing
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glastonbury
Festival">Glastonbury
Festival</a>.
The
band
also
released
the
breakthrough
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Yellow_(Coldplay_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yellow
(Coldplay
song)">Yellow</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-roach_42_24-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-roach_42-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
Having
the
role
as
Coldplay's
first
release
to
crack
the
top
five,
the
song
shot
to
number
four
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Singles
Chart">UK
Singles
Chart</a>
and
placed
Coldplay
in
public
consciousness.<sup
id="cite_ref-roach_42_24-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-roach_42-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Yellow&quot;
and
&quot;Shiver&quot;
were
initially
released
as
EPs
in
the
spring
of
2000.<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
former
was
later
released
as
a
single
in
United
Kingdom
on
26
June
2000.
In
the
United
States,
the
song
was
released
as
the
lead
single
from
the
then-untitled
debut
album.
In
October
2000,
the
track
was
sent
to
US
college
and
alternative
radio
outlets.<sup
id="cite_ref-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Coldplay
released
their
first
studio
album,
<i>Parachutes</i>,
on
10
July
2000
in
the
United
Kingdom
via
their
record
label,
<a
href="/wiki/Parlophone_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Parlophone
Records"
class="mw-redirect">Parlophone</a>.
The
album
debuted
at
number
one
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Albums
Chart">UK
Albums
Chart</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-roach_45_27-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-roach_45-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
released
on
7
November
2000
by
record
label
<a
href="/wiki/Nettwerk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nettwerk">Nettwerk</a>
in
North
America.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
has
been
made
available
on
various
formats
since
its
initial
release;
both
Parlophone
and
Nettwerk
released
it
as
a
CD
in
2000,
and
it
was
also
released
as
a
<a
href="/wiki/Compact_Cassette?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Compact
Cassette">cassette</a>
by
new
US
label
<a
href="/wiki/Capitol_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Capitol
Records">Capitol</a>
in
2001.
In
the
following
year,
Parlophone
issued
the
album
as
an
<a
href="/wiki/LP_record?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="LP
record">LP</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
released
a
limited-edition
CD
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Trouble_(Coldplay_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trouble
(Coldplay
song)">Trouble</a>&quot;,
the
third
single
from
the
album,
which
features
a
remix
of
&quot;Yellow&quot;.
It
was
pressed
to
1,000
copies,
and
was
issued
only
to
fans
and
journalists.<sup
id="cite_ref-MossHeats_0_30-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MossHeats_0-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
Both
&quot;Yellow&quot;
and
&quot;Trouble&quot;
earned
regular
radio
airplay
in
the
UK
and
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-AMGbio_31-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMGbio-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><i>Parachutes</i>
was
nominated
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Mercury_Music_Prize?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mercury
Music
Prize"
class="mw-redirect">Mercury
Music
Prize</a>
in
September
2000.<sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
Having
found
success
in
Europe,
the
band
set
their
sights
on
North
America,<sup
id="cite_ref-roach_76_33-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-roach_76-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
by
releasing
the
album
there
in
November
2000,
and
started
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/US_Club_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="US
Club
Tour">US
Club
Tour</a></i>
in
February
2001.<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the
2001
<a
href="/wiki/Brit_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brit
Awards">Brit
Awards</a>
in
February,
Coldplay
earned
awards
for
Best
British
Group,
and
Best
British
Album.<sup
id="cite_ref-ColdplayBrits_35-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ColdplayBrits-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
Although
<i>Parachutes</i>
was
a
slow-burning
success
in
the
United
States,
it
eventually
reached
double-platinum
status.<sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
critically
well
received
and
earned
a
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Alternative_Music_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Alternative
Music
Album">Best
Alternative
Music
Album</a>
honours
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/2002_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2002
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">2002
Grammy
Awards</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Grammy_wins_37-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Grammy_wins-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
Chris
Martin
claimed,
after
the
release
of
<i>Parachutes</i>,
that
the
album's
success
was
intended
to
elevate
the
band's
status
to
the
&quot;biggest,
best
band
in
the
world.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

Live
performances
during
their
2002
tour
were
noted
for
their
use
of











<a
href="/wiki/Strobe_light?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Strobe
light">strobe
lighting</a>.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>After
the
success
of
<i>Parachutes</i>,
Coldplay
returned
to
the
studio
in
September
2001
to
begin
work
on
their
second
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/A_Rush_of_Blood_to_the_Head?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Rush
of
Blood
to
the
Head">A
Rush
of
Blood
to
the
Head</a></i>,
once
again
with
Ken
Nelson
producing.
Since
the
band
had
never
stayed
in
London
before,
they
had
trouble
focusing.
They
decided
to
relocate
in
Liverpool,
where
they
recorded
some
of
the
songs
on
<i>Parachutes</i>.
Once
there,
vocalist
Chris
Martin
said
that
they
became
obsessed
with
recording.
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/In_My_Place?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
My
Place">In
My
Place</a>&quot;
was
the
first
song
recorded
for
the
album.
The
band
released
it
as
the
album's
lead
single
because
it
was
the
track
that
made
them
want
to
record
a
second
album
following
a
&quot;strange
period
of
not
really
knowing
what
we
were
doing&quot;
three
months
after
the
success
of
<i>Parachutes</i>.
According
to
Martin
&quot;one
thing
kept
us
going:
recording
'In
My
Place'.
Then
other
songs
started
coming.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-39"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
band
wrote
more
than
20
songs
for
the
album.
Some
of
their
new
material,
including
&quot;In
My
Place&quot;
and
&quot;Animals&quot;,
was
played
live
while
the
band
was
still
touring
<i>Parachutes</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-MossHeats_0_30-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MossHeats_0-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album's
title
was
revealed
through
a
post
on
the
band's
official
website.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
released
in
August
2002
and
spawned
several
popular
singles,
including
&quot;In
My
Place&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Clocks_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Clocks
(song)">Clocks</a>&quot;,
and
the
ballad
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Scientist_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Scientist
(song)">The
Scientist</a>&quot;.
The
latter
was
inspired
by
<a
href="/wiki/George_Harrison?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Harrison">George
Harrison</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/All_Things_Must_Pass_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
Things
Must
Pass
(song)">title
track
to
<i>All
Things
Must
Pass</i></a>,
which
was
released
in
1970.<sup
id="cite_ref-roach_98_42-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-roach_98-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Coldplay
toured
from
June
2002
to
September
2003
for
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/A_Rush_of_Blood_to_the_Head_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Rush
of
Blood
to
the
Head
Tour">A
Rush
of
Blood
to
the
Head
Tour</a></i>.
They
visited
five
continents,
including
co-headlining
festival
dates
at
<a
href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glastonbury
Festival">Glastonbury
Festival</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-roach_28_18-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-roach_28-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/V_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="V
Festival">V2003</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_Werchter?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
Werchter">Rock
Werchter</a>.
Many
concerts
showcased
elaborate
lighting
and
individualised
screens
reminiscent
of
U2's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Elevation_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elevation
Tour">Elevation
Tour</a></i>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Nine_Inch_Nails?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nine
Inch
Nails">Nine
Inch
Nails</a>'
<i><a
href="/wiki/Fragility_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fragility
Tour">Fragility
Tour</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
the
extended
tour,
Coldplay
recorded
a
live
DVD
and
CD,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Live_2003?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
2003">Live
2003</a></i>,
at
<a
href="/wiki/Sydney?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sydney">Sydney's</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Hordern_Pavilion?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hordern
Pavilion">Hordern
Pavilion</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the
2003
<a
href="/wiki/Brit_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brit
Awards">Brit
Awards</a>
held
at
<a
href="/wiki/Earls_Court_Exhibition_Centre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Earls
Court
Exhibition
Centre">Earls
Court</a>,
London,
Coldplay
received
awards
for
Best
British
Group,
and
Best
British
Album.<sup
id="cite_ref-ColdplayBrits_35-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ColdplayBrits-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
28
August
2003,
Coldplay
performed
&quot;The
Scientist&quot;
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/2003_MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2003
MTV
Video
Music
Awards">2003
MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Radio_City_Music_Hall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radio
City
Music
Hall">Radio
City
Music
Hall</a>
in
New
York
City,
and
won
three
awards.<sup
id="cite_ref-45"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
December
2003,
readers
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
chose
Coldplay
as
the
best
artist
and
the
best
band
of
the
year.<sup
id="cite_ref-46"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
that
time
the
band
covered
<a
href="/wiki/Pretenders_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pretenders
(band)"
class="mw-redirect">The
Pretenders</a>'
1983
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/2000_Miles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2000
Miles">2000
Miles</a>&quot;
(which
was
made
available
for
download
on
their
official
website).
&quot;2000
Miles&quot;
was
the
top
selling
UK
download
that
year,
with
proceeds
from
the
sales
donated
to
Future
Forests
and
Stop
Handgun
Violence
campaigns.<sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>A
Rush
of
Blood
to
the
Head</i>
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Alternative_Music_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Alternative
Music
Album">Grammy
Award
for
Best
Alternative
Music
Album</a>
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/2003_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2003
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">2003
Grammy
Awards</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-48"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the
<a
href="/wiki/2004_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2004
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">2004
Grammy
Awards</a>,
Coldplay
earned
<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy

for

for
&quot;Clocks&quot;.<sup

class="mw-headline"

(2004â€“06)</span>

class="mw-editsection">[<a

X&amp;Y
(2004â€“06)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div

<div

<div

<a

Coldplay
performing
in
Barcelona
during
their











<i><a
href="/wiki/Twisted_Logic_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Twisted
Logic
Tour">Twisted
Logic
Tour</a></i>
in
2005









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Coldplay
spent
most
of
2004
out
of
the
spotlight,
taking
a
break
from
touring
and
releasing
a
satire
music
video
of
a
song
from
a
fictional
band
titled
The
Nappies
while
recording
their
third
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-49"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i><a
href="/wiki/X%26Y?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="X&amp;Y">X&amp;Y</a></i>
was
released
in
June
2005
in
UK
and
Europe.<sup
id="cite_ref-50"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
new,
delayed
release
date
had
put
the
album
back
into
the
next
fiscal
year,
actually
causing
EMI's
stock
to
drop.<sup
id="cite_ref-51"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-52"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
became
the
best-selling
album
of
2005
with
worldwide
sales
of
8.3&nbsp;million.<sup
id="cite_ref-53"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
<a
href="/wiki/Lead_single?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lead
single">lead
single</a>,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Speed_of_Sound_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Speed
of
Sound
(song)">Speed
of
Sound</a>&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-54"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup>
made
its
radio
and
online
music
store
debut
on
18
April
and
was
released
as
a
CD
on
23
May
2005.<sup
id="cite_ref-55"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>X&amp;Y</i>
entered
the
album
charts
of
20
countries
at
the
number
one
position<sup
id="cite_ref-56"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
was
the
third-fastest
selling
album
in
UK
chart
history.<sup
id="cite_ref-57"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup>
Two
other
singles
were
released
that
year:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Fix_You?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fix
You">Fix
You</a>&quot;
in
September
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Talk_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Talk
(song)">Talk</a>&quot;
in
December.
Critical
reaction
to
<i>X&amp;Y</i>
was
mostly
positive,
though
slightly
less
enthusiastic
than
that
of
its
predecessor.
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
New
York
Times">The
New
York
Times</a></i>
critic
Jon
Pareles
described
Coldplay
as
&quot;the
most
insufferable
band
of
the
decade&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-58"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup>
whereas
<a
href="/wiki/NME?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NME">NME</a>
awarded
the
album
9/10
calling
it
&quot;Confident,
bold,
ambitious,
bunged
with
singles
and
impossible
to
contain,
'X&amp;Y'
doesn't
reinvent
the
wheel
but
it
does
reinforce
Coldplay
as
the
band
of
their
time&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-59"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Comparisons
between
Coldplay
and
<a
href="/wiki/U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2">U2</a>
became
increasingly
common.<sup
id="cite_ref-60"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Yahoo.21_61-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Yahoo.21-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup>
Chris
Martin
later
revealed
that
the
reviews
that
ranged
from
mixed
to
negative,
note-worthy
for
their
remarks
on
comparing
them
to
U2,
made
him
feel
&quot;liberated&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-62"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>From
June
2005
to
July
2006,
Coldplay
went
on
their
<i><a
href="/wiki/Twisted_Logic_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Twisted
Logic
Tour">Twisted
Logic
Tour</a></i>,
which
included
festival
dates
like
<a
href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Coachella
Valley
Music
and
Arts
Festival">Coachella</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Isle
of
Wight
Festival">Isle
of
Wight
Festival</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glastonbury
Festival">Glastonbury</a>
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Austin_City_Limits_Music_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Austin
City
Limits
Music
Festival">Austin
City
Limits
Music
Festival</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-63"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
July
2005,
the
band
appeared
at
<a
href="/wiki/Live_8?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
8">Live

in
<a
href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hyde
Park,
London">Hyde

where
they
played
a

of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Verve?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Verve">The
Verve</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Bitter_Sweet_Symphony?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bitter
Sweet
Symphony">Bitter

Symphony</a>&quot;
with
<a
href="/wiki/Richard_Ashcroft?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Richard
Ashcroft">Richard
Ashcroft</a>
on
vocals.<sup
id="cite_ref-64"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
28
August,
Coldplay
performed
&quot;Speed
of
Sound&quot;
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/2005_MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2005
MTV
Video
Music
Awards">2005
MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>
in
Miami.<sup
id="cite_ref-65"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup>
In

Coldplay
recorded
a
new
version
of
&quot;How
You
See
the
World&quot;
with
reworked

for
<a
href="/wiki/War_Child_(charity)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="War
Child
(charity)">War
Child</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/Help!:_A_Day_in_the_Life?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Help!:

in

A

in

charity
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-66"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup>
In

2006,

earned
Best
Album
and
Best
Single
honours
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Brit_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

Two

<p>In
October
2006,
Coldplay
began
work
on
their
fourth
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Viva_la_Vida_or_Death_and_All_His_Friends?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Viva
la
Vida
or
Death
and
All
His
Friends">Viva
la
Vida
or
Death
and
All
His
Friends</a></i>,
with
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Brian_Eno?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brian
Eno">Brian
Eno</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-69"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
Taking
a
break
from
recording,
the
band
<a
href="/wiki/Latin_America_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Latin
America
Tour"
class="mw-redirect">toured
Latin
America</a>
in
early
2007,
performing
in
Chile,
Argentina,
Brazil,
and
Mexico.<sup
id="cite_ref-70"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
recording
in
churches
and
other
venues
in
Latin
America
and
Spain
during
their
tour,
the
band
said
the
album
would
likely
reflect
<a
href="/wiki/Hispanic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a>
influence.<sup
id="cite_ref-71"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
group
spent
the
rest
of
the
year
recording
with
Eno.<sup
id="cite_ref-72"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

class="thumb
tright">









<div

Performing
live

<a

during

in

<p>Martin
described
<i>Viva
la
Vida</i>
as
a
new
direction
for
Coldplay:
a
change
from
their
past
three
albums,
which
they
have
referred
to
as
a
&quot;trilogy&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-different_73-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-different-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
said
the
album
featured
less
<a
href="/wiki/Falsetto?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Falsetto">falsetto</a>
as
he
allowed
his
voice's
lower
register
to
take
precedence.<sup
id="cite_ref-different_73-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-different-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup>
Some
songs,
such
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Violet_Hill_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Violet
Hill
(song)">Violet
Hill</a>&quot;,
contain
distorted
guitar
<a
href="/wiki/Riff?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Riff"
class="mw-redirect">riffs</a>
and
bluesy
undertones.<sup
id="cite_ref-different_73-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-different-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>&quot;Violet
Hill&quot;
was
confirmed
as
the
first
single,
with
a
radio
release
date
of
29
April
2008.<sup
id="cite_ref-74"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
the
first
play,
it
was
freely
obtainable
from
Coldplay's
website
from
12:15&nbsp;pm&nbsp;(GMT&nbsp;+0)
for
one
week
(achieving
two
million
downloads),<sup
id="cite_ref-75"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup>
until
it
became
commercially
available
to
download
on
6
May.<sup
id="cite_ref-76"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-77"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Violet
Hill&quot;
entered
the
UK
Top
10,
US
Top
40
(entering
the
Top
10
in
the
Hot
Modern
Rock
Tracks
chart)
and
charted
well
in
the
rest
of
the
world.<sup
id="cite_ref-78"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
title
track,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Viva_la_Vida?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Viva
la
Vida">Viva
la
Vida</a>&quot;,
was
also
released
exclusively
on
iTunes.
It
became
the
band's
first
number
one
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100"><i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-79"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
their
first
UK
number
one,
based
on
download
sales
alone.<sup
id="cite_ref-80"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
was
also
the
first
Number
One
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Singles
Chart">UK
Singles
Chart</a>
to
be
based
solely
on
download
sales.</p>








<p>Upon
release,
<i>Viva
la
Vida
or
Death
and
All
His
Friends</i>
topped
the
album
charts
worldwide,
and
was
the
world's
best-selling
album
of
2008.<sup
id="cite_ref-81"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
hit
number
one
on
the
UK
album
chart,
despite
having
come
on
the
market
only
three
days
previously.
In
that
time,
it
sold
302,000
copies;
the
BBC
called
it
&quot;one
of
the
fastest-selling
records
in
UK
history&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-82"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup>
By
the
end
of
June,
it
had
set
a
new
record
for
most-downloaded
album
ever.<sup
id="cite_ref-83"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-84"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
October
2008,
Coldplay
won
two
<a
href="/wiki/Q_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Q
Awards"><i>Q</i>
Awards</a>
for
Best
Album
for
<i>Viva
la
Vida
or
Death
and
All
His
Friends</i>
and
Best
Act
in
the
World
Today.<sup
id="cite_ref-85"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
9
November,
Coldplay
were
named
the
World's
Best
Selling
Act
of
2008
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/2008_World_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2008
World
Music
Awards">World
Music
Awards</a>
in
Monte
Carlo.<sup
id="cite_ref-86"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
also
picked
up
two
other
awards,
World's
Best
Selling
Rock
Act
and
Great
Britain's
Best
Selling
Act.<sup
id="cite_ref-87"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
followed
up
<i>Viva
la
Vida
or
Death
and
All
His
Friends</i>
with
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Prospekt%27s_March_EP?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Prospekt's
March
EP"
class="mw-redirect">Prospekt's
March
EP</a></i>,
which
was
released
on
21
November
2008.
The
EP
features
tracks
from
the
<i>Viva
la
Vida
or
Death
and
All
His
Friends</i>
sessions
and,<sup
id="cite_ref-MTV.com_88-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MTV.com-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-89"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup>
as
well
as
being
available
on
its
own,
was
issued
as
a
bonus
disc
with
later
editions
of
<i>Viva
la
Vida
or
Death
and
All
His
Friends</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-90"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Life_in_Technicolor_II?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Life
in
Technicolor
II">Life
in
Technicolor
II</a>&quot;
was
the
only
single
released
from
the
EP.</p>

<p>Coldplay
began
their
<i>Viva
la
Vida
Tour</i>
in
June,
with
a
free
concert
at
Brixton
Academy
in
London.<sup
id="cite_ref-91"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
was
followed
two
days
later
by
a
45-minute
performance
that
was
broadcast
live
from
outside
<a
href="/wiki/BBC_Television_Centre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BBC
Television
Centre">BBC
Television
Centre</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-92"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup>
Released
in
late
2008,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lost!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lost!">Lost!</a>&quot;
became
the
third
single
from
the
album,
featuring
a
new
version
with
<a
href="/wiki/Jay-Z?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>.
After
performing
the
opening
set
on
14
March
2009
for
<a
href="/wiki/Sound_Relief?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sound
Relief">Sound
Relief</a>
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Sydney_Cricket_Ground?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sydney
Cricket
Ground">Sydney
Cricket
Ground</a>,
Coldplay
headlined
a
sold-out
concert
later
that
same
night.<sup
id="cite_ref-Mitchell_93-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Mitchell-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup>
Sound
Relief
is
a
benefit
concert
for
victims
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Black_Saturday_bushfires?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Saturday
bushfires">Victorian
Bushfire
Crisis</a>
and
the
Queensland
<a
href="/wiki/Flood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Flood">Floods</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-94"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
4
December
2008,
<a
href="/wiki/Joe_Satriani?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joe
Satriani">Joe
Satriani</a>
filed
a
<a
href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Copyright
infringement">copyright
infringement</a>
suit
against
Coldplay
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Central_District_of_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="United
States
District
Court
for
the
Central
District
of
California">United
States
District
Court
for
the
Central
District
of
California</a>.
Satriani's
suit
asserted
that
the
Coldplay
song
&quot;Viva
la
Vida&quot;
includes
&quot;substantial
original
portions&quot;
of
the
Satriani
song
&quot;If
I
Could
Fly&quot;
from
his
2004
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Is_There_Love_in_Space%3F?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Is
There
Love
in
Space?">Is
There
Love
in
Space?</a></i>.
The
Coldplay
song
in
question
received
two
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Awards</a>
for
&quot;Song
of
the
Year.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-95"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
denied
the
allegation.<sup
id="cite_ref-96"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-97"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup>
An
unspecified
settlement
was
ultimately
reached
between
the
parties.<sup
id="cite_ref-98"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Coldplay
were
nominated
for
four
BRIT
Awards
in
2009:
British
Group,
British
Live
Act,
British
Single
(&quot;Viva
la
Vida&quot;)
and
British
Album
(<i>Viva
la
Vida
or
Death
and
All
His
Friends</i>).<sup
id="cite_ref-99"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the
<a
href="/wiki/51st_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="51st
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">51st
Grammy
Awards</a>
in
the
same
year,
Coldplay
won
three
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Awards</a>
in
the
categories
for
Song
of
Year
for
&quot;Viva
la
Vida&quot;,
Best
Rock
Album
for
<i>Viva
la
Vida
or
Death
and
All
His
Friends</i>,
and
Best
Vocal
Pop
Performance
by
a
Duo
or
Group
for
&quot;Viva
la
Vida&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-100"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-101"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>A
live
album
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/LeftRightLeftRightLeft?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="LeftRightLeftRightLeft">LeftRightLeftRightLeft</a></i>
was
recorded
at
various
shows
during
the
tour.
<i>LeftRightLeftRightLeft</i>,
released
on
15
May
2009,
was
to
be
given
away
at

concerts
of
their
<i>Viva
la
Vida</i>

It
was
also

as

<a

Following
the
<i><a

title="Viva
la
Vida
Tour">Viva
la
Vida
Tour</a></i>,
Coldplay
announced
another
&quot;Latin
America

to

in

href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup>

won
Song
of
the
Year
for
&quot;Viva
la
Vida&quot;
at
<a
href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Composers,_Authors_and_Publishers?qsrc=3044"

Society
of

and

Society
of

(ASCAP)
Awards
in
London.<sup
id="cite_ref-104"
class="reference"><a

In

<i><a

<p>The
band
finished
recording
the
new
album
in
mid-2011.
When
Martin
and
Champion
were
interviewed
by
BBC
Radio
and
asked
about
the
album's
lyrical
themes,
Martin
replied
&quot;It's
about
love,
addiction,
<a
href="/wiki/Obsessive_compulsive_disorder?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Obsessive
compulsive
disorder"
class="mw-redirect">OCD</a>,
escape
and
working
for
someone
you
don't
like.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-105"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup>
When
asked
whether
or
not
their
fifth
album
would
be
out
by
the
summer,
Martin
and
Champion
said
that
there
was
plenty
of
work
to
be
done
before
releasing
it.
They
confirmed
several
festival
appearances
before
its
release
date,
especially
a
headlining
spot
in
the
2011
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_Werchter?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
Werchter">Rock
Werchter</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Pinkpop_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pinkpop
Festival">Pinkpop
Festival</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glastonbury
Festival">Glastonbury
Festival</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/T_in_the_Park?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="T
in
the
Park">T
in
the
Park</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Austin_City_Limits_Music_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Austin
City
Limits
Music

<p>On

(Coldplay

<i>Mylo

to

to

in

<p>On

href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
Coldplay's
live
show
at
the
iTunes
Festival,
Coldplay
played
four
of
their
new
songs,
Always
in
my
Head,
Magic,
Another's
Arms,
and
Midnight.</p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Musical_style">Musical
style</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Coldplay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
Musical
style">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Coldplay's
frontman
Chris
Martin
once
proclaimed
the
band's
music
as
&quot;limestone
rock&quot;
in
comparison
to
&quot;hard
rock&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-139"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band's
music
has
been
called
&quot;meditative&quot;
and
&quot;blue
romantic&quot;;
it
&quot;[reflects]
on
their
emotions&quot;
and
Martin
&quot;endlessly
examine[s]
his
feelings&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-x.26y_140-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-x.26y-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup>
Martin's
lyrical
wordplay
has
been
called
feminist,
similar
to
<a
href="/wiki/Andrew_Montgomery?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Andrew
Montgomery">Andrew
Montgomery</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Geneva_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Geneva
(band)">Geneva</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-parachutes_141-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-parachutes-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

class="mbox-small"

<p>In
the
late
1990s,
the
EPs
released
by
the
band
had
characteristics
of
<a
href="/wiki/Dream_pop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dream
pop">dream
pop</a>,
setting
them
apart
from
later
studio
albums.
The
tone
of
the
band's
first
studio
album,
<i>Parachutes</i>,
was
described
as
melodic
pop
with
&quot;distorted
guitar
riffs
and
swishing
percussion&quot;
but
also
being
&quot;exquisitely
dark
and
artistically
abrasive&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-parachutes_141-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-parachutes-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup>
Such
<a
href="/wiki/Alternative_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alternative
rock">alternative
rock</a>
style
has
been
compared
to
bands
like
<a
href="/wiki/U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2">U2</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Oasis_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Oasis
(band)">Oasis</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Radiohead?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Travis_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Travis
(band)">Travis</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-parachutes_141-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-parachutes-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-142"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
acknowledges
the
Scottish
alternative
rock
band,
<a
href="/wiki/Travis_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Travis
(band)">Travis</a>,
as
a
major
influence
on
their
earlier
material.<sup
id="cite_ref-Travis_143-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Travis-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
their
second
studio
album
<i>A
Rush
of
Blood
to
the
Head</i>,
the
band
draws
inspiration
from
artists
like
<a
href="/wiki/Echo_%26_the_Bunnymen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Echo
&amp;
the
Bunnymen">Echo
&amp;
the
Bunnymen</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-roach_18_144-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-roach_18-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Kate_Bush?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kate
Bush">Kate
Bush</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/George_Harrison?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Harrison">George
Harrison</a><sup
id="cite_ref-roach_98_42-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-roach_98-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Muse_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Muse
(band)">Muse</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-145"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
songs
in
it
were
considered
to
contain
&quot;lush
melodies
and
a
heartbreak&quot;
and
that
they
had
a
&quot;newfound
confidence.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-rush_146-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rush-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
music
on
their
third
release
<i>X&amp;Y</i>
has
been
considered
to
be
&quot;ruminations
on
Martin's
doubts,
fears,
hopes,
and
loves.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-x.26y_140-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-x.26y-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
particularly
influenced
by
the
artists
<a
href="/wiki/Johnny_Cash?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Johnny
Cash">Johnny
Cash</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Kraftwerk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kraftwerk">Kraftwerk</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-147"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
<i><a
href="/wiki/Viva_la_Vida_or_Death_and_All_His_Friends?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Viva
la
Vida
or
Death
and
All
His
Friends">Viva
la
Vida
or
Death
and
All
His
Friends</a></i>,
the
group's
style
was
moving
towards
<a
href="/wiki/Art_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Art
rock">art
rock</a>,
being
influenced
by
the
bands
<a
href="/wiki/Blur_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blur
(band)">Blur</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Arcade_Fire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Arcade
Fire">Arcade
Fire</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/My_Bloody_Valentine_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="My
Bloody
Valentine
(band)">My
Bloody
Valentine</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-148"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
experimented
with
different
instruments
including
orchestras,
honky-tonk
pianos
and
further
so.<sup
id="cite_ref-149"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-150"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mylo_Xyloto?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mylo
Xyloto">Mylo
Xyloto</a></i>
carries
the
concept
album
format
from
the
love
and
war-induced
<i>Viva
la
Vida</i>
and
expands
the
spectrum
to
include
electronic
and
acoustic
elements.
Lyrical
influences
were
taken
from
<a
href="/wiki/Graffiti?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Graffiti">graffiti</a>
and
the
German
resistance
group
<a
href="/wiki/White_Rose?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="White
Rose">White
Rose</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-151"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Regarding
their
international
wide
success,
the
band's
president
at
Parlophone,
<a
href="/wiki/Miles_Leonard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Miles
Leonard">Miles
Leonard</a>
has
stated
that
one
of
their
&quot;secrets&quot;
is
that
they
have
never
sounded
like
a
parochial
UK
artist,
saying:
&quot;Some
bands
are
very
proud
to
be
British,
but
sometimes
come
across
as
being
very
â€˜Britishâ€™.
Coldplay
never
aspire
to
that;
on
one
hand
they
sound
British
but
on
the
other
they
sound
like
a
huge
global
artist.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-hitquarters.com_112-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-hitquarters.com-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2011
Coldplay
were
hailed
as
'Rock
Statesmen'.<sup
id="cite_ref-152"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
